If TypeScript adds too much complexity, use JavaScript with the same logical structure.

==================================================
3D ASSETS / PLACEHOLDERS
==================================================

If real models are unavailable, create polished procedural placeholders:

Cups:
- use Babylon mesh primitives
- cylinder/frustum style
- metallic/ceramic material
- rounded illusion with highlights

Table:
- box mesh with warm wood material
- subtle procedural texture

Money:
- thin rectangular planes/boxes
- paper dollar texture-like green material
- stacked with slight offsets

Whiskey:
- transparent glass cylinder
- amber liquid cylinder
- subtle highlight

Ball:
- small glossy sphere

Hands:
- stylized simplified mesh placeholders
- acceptable as simple rig-like shapes
- should still move convincingly

CV documents:
- thin paper planes
- folder plane/box
- stamped labels as textures or React overlay aligned to screen

Environment:
- skybox or large background planes
- tropical ocean image placeholder using gradients if no assets
- palm silhouettes / soft background layers

==================================================
ANIMATION REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

Use Babylon animation system or custom tweening.

Required animations:
- arrival camera pan from ocean to table
- whiskey glass lift/sip/place animation
- cup shuffle animation
- dealer hand movement during shuffle
- cup lift animation
- money slide to player
- money removed from player
- money moved to pending area
- fraud hand reveal
- bonus keep/switch reveal
- final folder placement
- document page turn/slide

Animations should feel smooth, cinematic, and intentional.

No teleporting objects unless hidden by camera/misdirection.

==================================================
ADVANCED GUI REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

The GUI must look premium.

Include:
- animated subtitle bar
- right-corner insight card
- smooth scene transitions
- hover/click effects
- subtle vignette
- soft blur panels
- interaction prompts
- CV document overlays
- responsive layout
- mobile fallback warning if needed

Do not make it look like plain HTML buttons.

==================================================
GITHUB PAGES DEPLOYMENT
==================================================

Add or update:

vite.config.js

Use:

import { defineConfig } from 'vite'
import react from '@vitejs/plugin-react'

export default defineConfig({
plugins: [react()],
base: '/igaming-shell-cv/',
})

Add GitHub Actions workflow:

.github/workflows/deploy.yml

Use:
- actions/checkout@v4
- actions/setup-node@v4
- actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
- actions/deploy-pages@v4

Workflow:
- trigger on push to main
- npm ci
- npm run build
- upload dist
- deploy to GitHub Pages

==================================================
PACKAGE DEPENDENCIES
==================================================

Install:
- react
- react-dom
- vite
- @vitejs/plugin-react
- typescript if using TS
- tailwindcss
- postcss
- autoprefixer
- @babylonjs/core
- @babylonjs/loaders
- framer-motion
- lucide-react

If Tailwind is not configured, configure it.

tailwind.config.js should include:

content: [
"./index.html",
"./src/**/*.{js,jsx,ts,tsx}",
]

src/index.css should include:

@tailwind base;
@tailwind components;
@tailwind utilities;

==================================================
ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA
==================================================

The final project is acceptable if:

- Password gate appears first
- Correct password unlocks the story
- WebGPU renderer is attempted first
- WebGL fallback works if WebGPU is unavailable
- Experience is 3D first-person, not flat UI
- Background is warm, tropical, premium, and light
- Noir exists in dialogue only, not as a dark visual theme
- Intro starts by looking at ocean
- Whiskey glass is lifted, sipped, and placed on table
- Camera transitions to first-person table view
- Dealer and player communicate through short subtitles
- No candidate info appears during gameplay
- Right-corner product insights appear subtly
- Money is physical paper dollars on the table
- No numeric score or bankroll is shown
- Each scene represents a product domain
- Fraud scene lets player click either cup or dealer hand
- Bonus scene offers keep/switch choice
- CV appears only at the end as a confidential folder/documents
- CV pages include NDA/confidential marks
- Contact page includes volk.na.oxote@gmail.com
- App builds with npm run build
- GitHub Pages workflow is included

==================================================
IMPORTANT VISUAL PRIORITY
==================================================

Do not implement this as a basic React card layout.

The main value is the 3D cinematic table scene:
- ocean intro
- whiskey
- warm table
- cups
- dealer hands
- paper dollars
- subtle misdirection
- final CV folder

React UI should support the story, not replace the scene.Create a WebGPU-first 3D interactive web experience.

Project title:
“Guess the Cup. Read the Product.”

Goal:
Build a cinematic first-person 3D shell-game story that works as a creative CV / product case presentation for an iGaming Business Analyst / Product BA candidate.

This should NOT be a normal resume website.
This should NOT be an arcade game.
This should NOT be a neon casino UI.

It should feel like:
- a private tropical table game
- a warm cinematic product conversation
- a magic trick with misdirection
- noir humor in dialogue only
- advanced WebGPU/WebGL 3D scene
- subtle business/product insights
- CV revealed only at the end as documents on the table

==================================================
TECH STACK
==================================================

Use:

- React
- Vite
- TypeScript if practical, otherwise JavaScript
- Babylon.js for 3D scene
- WebGPU-first rendering
- WebGL fallback if WebGPU is unavailable
- Tailwind CSS for UI overlays
- Framer Motion for UI transitions
- lucide-react only for small UI icons if needed

The 3D scene must be handled by Babylon.js.
React should handle:
- password gate
- subtitles
- right-corner insight cards
- interaction prompts
- CV document text overlays
- contact buttons

The app must be static and deployable to GitHub Pages.

Repository name:

igaming-shell-cv

Use this in vite.config.js:

base: '/igaming-shell-cv/'

==================================================
WEBGPU / WEBGL REQUIREMENT
==================================================

Implement rendering like this:

1. Try to initialize Babylon.js WebGPU engine.
2. If WebGPU is unavailable, gracefully fall back to Babylon.js WebGL engine.
3. If neither works, show a polished fallback message:
“Your browser cannot run this private table. Try a modern desktop browser.”

Important:
Do not make WebGPU-only with no fallback.

Show a tiny non-intrusive technical badge only if needed:
- “WebGPU mode”
- “WebGL fallback mode”

But keep it subtle.

==================================================
PASSWORD GATE
==================================================

Before the story starts, show a full-screen password screen.

Title:
Private Product Demo

Subtitle:
A small shell game about iGaming product logic, risk, payments, and requirements.

Password:
iGamingBA2026!

Do NOT show the password visibly.

Use SHA-256 comparison with browser Web Crypto API.

SHA-256 hash:
2834c295eb954847ae5538f997d4970ce4b55fc07d8ad400a73d2a7ea335de0a

If correct:
- store unlocked state in sessionStorage
- show the story

If wrong:
show error:
“Wrong cup. Wrong password. Product risk detected.”

Microcopy:
“Demo access only.”

Add comment near password logic:
“Frontend password protection is only a demo barrier for static hosting. Do not use this for sensitive or NDA-protected information.”

Password page visual style:
- warm tropical
- glassmorphism
- elegant
- soft light
- muted amber / sand / tropical green
- not dark hacker
- not neon casino

==================================================
OVERALL STORY FORMAT
==================================================

Create a linear cinematic story.

Flow:

Password Gate
→ Arrival / Ocean Intro
→ First-Person Table View
→ Scene 1: Player Lifecycle
→ Scene 2: Provider Influence
→ Scene 3: KYC
→ Scene 4: Fraud Awareness
→ Scene 5: Bonus Mechanics
→ Scene 6: Payments / Cashier
→ Scene 7: Risk & Compliance
→ Final Hand
→ CV Folder Reveal
→ CV Pages
→ Contact / Replay

The user should not freely move around.
Use a fixed first-person camera with controlled cinematic camera movements.

==================================================
VISUAL DIRECTION
==================================================

The scene is 3D, first-person, warm, light, tropical, premium, and cinematic.

Visual mood:
- tropical terrace
- ocean in the distance
- warm daylight or soft sunset
- palm leaves
- warm wooden table
- whiskey glass
- paper dollars
- elegant cups
- subtle shadows
- soft depth
- calm luxury
- mature private game atmosphere

Important:
The “noir” should exist in the dialogue and jokes only.
The visual background should be warm and light, not dark noir.

Avoid:
- dark cyber/hacker theme
- neon casino
- childish arcade style
- heavy black UI
- loud comedy
- large text blocks during gameplay
- visible candidate/CV content before the final folder reveal

The game should look like:
“a private product conversation disguised as a shell game.”

==================================================
3D SCENE COMPOSITION
==================================================

Create a first-person table scene.

Camera:
- fixed seated position
- looks slightly downward at table
- can slowly pan/tilt during story moments
- should feel like the player is sitting at the table

Recommended camera:
- position: x 0, y 1.25, z -3.2
- rotation: slight downward angle
- FOV: 45–55

Scene objects:
- tropical ocean / terrace background
- palm leaves / greenery
- warm wooden table
- dealer area opposite player
- 3 cups in center
- small ball
- paper dollars near player
- paper dollars near dealer
- whiskey glass near player
- optional cigar case / lighter / small luxury props
- dealer hands
- optional subtle player hands at bottom
- CV folder/documents for final scene

Use placeholder 3D models if needed, but make them visually polished:
- cups should be 3D objects, not flat UI
- money should be paper bills lying on the table
- whiskey glass should be visible in intro and table view
- dealer hands can be stylized 3D models or simplified mesh placeholders

==================================================
MONEY RULES
==================================================

Do NOT show numeric score.
Do NOT show bankroll number.
Do NOT show points.

Money must be physical paper dollars on the table.

Player should see:
- paper dollars near player
- paper dollars near dealer
- money moving physically across the table

Money animations:
- dealer gives dollars to player
- dealer takes dollars from player
- dealer leaves some money
- dealer moves money to pending area
- dealer gives whiskey as soft compensation
- money stack visually grows or shrinks

Use money as a visual story object, not a counter.

==================================================
TEXT RULES DURING GAMEPLAY
==================================================

During gameplay:
- do NOT show candidate information
- do NOT explain the resume
- do NOT show big text blocks
- do NOT show long lessons

Only show:
1. short subtitle dialogue at the bottom
2. small right-corner product insight
3. short interaction prompts

Subtitle style:
- bottom center
- cinematic
- short lines
- speaker name in muted amber
- text in warm white
- dark translucent box
- optional typewriter effect

Right-corner insight style:
- small
- elegant
- subtle
- business/product hint
- not distracting
- changes depending on scene and outcome

==================================================
DIALOGUE STYLE
==================================================

Tone:
- mature
- intelligent
- dry
- noir jokes
- understated humor
- confident
- calm
- not childish
- not clownish
- not too theatrical

Dealer personality:
- smooth
- observant
- ironic
- slightly manipulative
- calm

Player personality:
- sharp
- calm
- capable
- not naive

Examples:
- “Luck is a polite word for weak planning.”
- “Trust is expensive. Friction is too.”
- “You watched the cups. I watched your attention.”
- “A good bonus doesn’t feel desperate.”
- “Verification begins where charm stops working.”

Never mock gambling addiction or vulnerable users.
Jokes should target:
- bad product logic
- weak controls
- unclear requirements
- payment ambiguity
- stakeholder optimism

==================================================
ARRIVAL / OCEAN INTRO
==================================================

Initial scene:
- no text at first
- camera looks far toward the ocean
- warm tropical terrace
- soft ambience
- a hand lifts a whiskey glass
- takes a small sip
- gently places the glass on the wooden table
- camera slowly pans / moves down into the primary table view

Then subtitle appears:

Dealer:
“You’re just in time.”

Camera settles into first-person table view.

==================================================
CORE INTERACTION MODEL
==================================================

Use Babylon.js picking/raycasting.

Interactive objects:
- cups
- dealer hand during fraud scene
- Keep / Switch choice during bonus scene
- Continue prompt
- CV document pages
- Contact buttons via React UI

Interaction rules:
- cups clickable only during choice moments
- dealer hand clickable only during fraud scene
- continue button advances after each scene result
- keep/switch buttons appear only during bonus scene
- CV pages turn with Next / Previous
- replay restarts story after password remains unlocked
- no numeric score
- money changes physically

==================================================
SCENE 1 — PLAYER LIFECYCLE
==================================================

Product domain:
Player lifecycle / retention / return behavior

Setup:
Dealer starts shaking / sliding the cups.

Dialogue:
Dealer: “How long has it been?”
Player: “Three… four months, maybe.”
Dealer: “Long enough to forget the odds. Not long enough to forget the feeling.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: Lifecycle Insight
Text: Returning players are shaped by timing, previous experience, offer relevance, and friction.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

If correct:
- reveal ball
- dealer gives paper dollars to player
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Still sharp. I like that.”
- right-corner insight changes:
Early positive outcomes can increase session intent and willingness to continue.

If wrong:
- dealer takes some money
- leaves some money on player side
- slides or signals an extra whiskey
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Bad luck. Let’s not make it dramatic.”
- right-corner insight changes:
Loss recovery offers can reduce drop-off when they feel personal rather than desperate.

==================================================
SCENE 2 — PROVIDER INFLUENCE
==================================================

Product domain:
Provider quality / game content / partner performance

Dialogue:
Dealer: “Do you remember who introduced us?”
Player: “I remember enough.”
Dealer: “Good. Some introductions are worth keeping. Some are just traffic with a logo.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: Provider Insight
Text: Provider quality affects session depth, discovery, trust, and content performance.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer gives money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Good choice. Some names know how to keep a table busy.”
- insight:
Strong content mix can improve engagement beyond acquisition traffic.

Wrong:
- dealer takes money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Not every shiny table pays for the room.”
- insight:
Weak provider performance can reduce engagement even when acquisition looks healthy.

==================================================
SCENE 3 — KYC
==================================================

Product domain:
KYC / identity / verification / friction / trust

Dialogue:
Player: “Do you even know who I am?”
Dealer: “Enough to let you sit. Not enough to let you disappear.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: KYC Insight
Text: Verification is a trust layer, but poor timing and friction can damage conversion.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer gives money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Clean papers. Clean hands. Rare combination.”

Wrong:
- dealer takes money or delays payout
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Identity is easy. Trust is expensive.”

Hidden product meaning:
KYC is not only compliance. It affects conversion, trust, and continuation.

==================================================
SCENE 4 — FRAUD AWARENESS
==================================================

Product domain:
Fraud / abuse cases / suspicious behavior / misdirection

Important:
No falling-ball mechanic.

New mechanic:
Dealer uses tricky hands and secretly hides the ball in his hand.

Player can click:
1. a cup
2. the dealer’s hand

If player clicks the hand:
- dealer reveals the ball in his hand
- no money is taken
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Checking my hands? Cute.”
Dealer: “Good. You were watching the system, not the decoration.”
- insight:
Fraud often happens outside the obvious user path. Detection depends on behavior, timing, and anomalies.

If player clicks a cup:
- dealer opens hand and shows the ball was never under the cups
- dealer laughs softly
- no money is taken
- subtitle:
Dealer: “You watched the cups.”
Dealer: “I watched your attention.”
- insight:
Fraud patterns often hide in transitions, exceptions, and trusted flows.

Meaning:
This scene teaches that fraud is about attention, misdirection, abuse paths, and suspicious behavior outside the obvious interface.

==================================================
SCENE 5 — BONUS MECHANICS
==================================================

Product domain:
Bonus design / incentive logic / choice architecture

Setup:
Player chooses a cup.

Then dealer slowly lifts another cup slightly and offers a second decision.

Dialogue:
Dealer: “You can keep what you chose.”
Dealer: “Or make it interesting.”

Player choices:
- Keep
- Switch

If player keeps:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Discipline. Rare quality.”
- insight:
A good bonus respects player confidence without forcing unnecessary risk.

If player switches:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition. Expensive habit.”
- insight:
Bonus design balances excitement, cost, abuse risk, and long-term player value.

If switch wins:
- dealer gives more money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambitious. I respect that.”

If switch loses:
- dealer takes some money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition sends invoices.”

==================================================
SCENE 6 — PAYMENTS / CASHIER
==================================================

Product domain:
Payments / cashier / withdrawal logic

Dialogue:
Player: “You pay immediately?”
Dealer: “Only when the system knows what it owes.”

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer pushes dollars clearly across table
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Fast payout. Dangerous thing. People start trusting you.”
- insight:
Clear payout states build trust and reduce support pressure.

Wrong:
- money stays in the middle / pending area
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Pending.”
Player: “That sounds expensive.”
Dealer: “Usually for support.”
- insight:
Every unclear payment state becomes support load: pending, approved, declined, reversed, refunded, manual review.

Required states to show or mention in insight:
- pending
- approved
- declined
- reversed
- refunded
- manual review

==================================================
SCENE 7 — RISK & COMPLIANCE
==================================================

Product domain:
Risk, compliance, auditability

Dialogue:
Dealer: “Rules are boring until someone asks for proof.”
Player: “And then?”
Dealer: “Then boring becomes expensive.”

Interaction:
Short shell-game decision or document/card choice.

Insight:
Good product logic leaves evidence: decisions, states, actions, ownership, and audit trails.

Money movement:
Keep subtle.
If correct, dealer taps the table and leaves money untouched.
If wrong, one dollar moves to a “review” area.

==================================================
FINAL HAND
==================================================

Product domain:
Judgment / product decision-making

Dialogue:
Dealer: “One last hand.”
Player: “For money?”
Dealer: “For judgment.”

Run one final quick cup choice.

After result:
Dealer: “The game is over.”
Dealer: “The product questions are not.”

Dealer places a folder on the table.

==================================================
CV FOLDER REVEAL
==================================================

After gameplay, the CV appears.

This is the first place where more text is acceptable.

Animation:
- dealer places a folder on the table
- folder has stamp:
CONFIDENTIAL
PRODUCT BA PROFILE
- player can click “Next Page”
- page turns / slides / flips
- each page looks like a physical document
- NDA stamps appear on some sections
- text can be longer here

Subtitle:
Dealer: “Take a look.”
Dealer: “Tell me if this man fits the job.”

NDA humor:
Dealer: “He keeps secrets.”
Dealer: “Useful, if your business has sensitive corners.”

- WebGL fallback works if WebGPU is unavailable
- Experience is 3D first-person, not flat UI
- Background is warm, tropical, premium, and light
- Noir exists in dialogue only, not as a dark visual theme
- Intro starts by looking at ocean
- Whiskey glass is lifted, sipped, and placed on table
- Camera transitions to first-person table view
- Dealer and player communicate through short subtitles
- No candidate info appears during gameplay
- Right-corner product insights appear subtly
- Money is physical paper dollars on the table
- No numeric score or bankroll is shown
- Each scene represents a product domain
- Fraud scene lets player click either cup or dealer hand
- Bonus scene offers keep/switch choice
- CV appears only at the end as a confidential folder/documents
- CV pages include NDA/confidential marks
- Contact page includes volk.na.oxote@gmail.com
- App builds with npm run build
- GitHub Pages workflow is included

==================================================
IMPORTANT VISUAL PRIORITY
==================================================

Do not implement this as a basic React card layout.

The main value is the 3D cinematic table scene:
- ocean intro
- whiskey
- warm table
- cups
- dealer hands
- paper dollars
- subtle misdirection
- final CV folder

React UI should support the story, not replace the scene.Create a WebGPU-first 3D interactive web experience.

Project title:
“Guess the Cup. Read the Product.”

Goal:
Build a cinematic first-person 3D shell-game story that works as a creative CV / product case presentation for an iGaming Business Analyst / Product BA candidate.

This should NOT be a normal resume website.
This should NOT be an arcade game.
This should NOT be a neon casino UI.

It should feel like:
- a private tropical table game
- a warm cinematic product conversation
- a magic trick with misdirection
- noir humor in dialogue only
- advanced WebGPU/WebGL 3D scene
- subtle business/product insights
- CV revealed only at the end as documents on the table

==================================================
TECH STACK
==================================================

Use:

- React
- Vite
- TypeScript if practical, otherwise JavaScript
- Babylon.js for 3D scene
- WebGPU-first rendering
- WebGL fallback if WebGPU is unavailable
- Tailwind CSS for UI overlays
- Framer Motion for UI transitions
- lucide-react only for small UI icons if needed

The 3D scene must be handled by Babylon.js.
React should handle:
- password gate
- subtitles
- right-corner insight cards
- interaction prompts
- CV document text overlays
- contact buttons

The app must be static and deployable to GitHub Pages.

Repository name:

igaming-shell-cv

Use this in vite.config.js:

base: '/igaming-shell-cv/'

==================================================
WEBGPU / WEBGL REQUIREMENT
==================================================

Implement rendering like this:

1. Try to initialize Babylon.js WebGPU engine.
2. If WebGPU is unavailable, gracefully fall back to Babylon.js WebGL engine.
3. If neither works, show a polished fallback message:
“Your browser cannot run this private table. Try a modern desktop browser.”

Important:
Do not make WebGPU-only with no fallback.

Show a tiny non-intrusive technical badge only if needed:
- “WebGPU mode”
- “WebGL fallback mode”

But keep it subtle.

==================================================
PASSWORD GATE
==================================================

Before the story starts, show a full-screen password screen.

Title:
Private Product Demo

Subtitle:
A small shell game about iGaming product logic, risk, payments, and requirements.

Password:
iGamingBA2026!

Do NOT show the password visibly.

Use SHA-256 comparison with browser Web Crypto API.

SHA-256 hash:
2834c295eb954847ae5538f997d4970ce4b55fc07d8ad400a73d2a7ea335de0a

If correct:
- store unlocked state in sessionStorage
- show the story

If wrong:
show error:
“Wrong cup. Wrong password. Product risk detected.”

Microcopy:
“Demo access only.”

Add comment near password logic:
“Frontend password protection is only a demo barrier for static hosting. Do not use this for sensitive or NDA-protected information.”

Password page visual style:
- warm tropical
- glassmorphism
- elegant
- soft light
- muted amber / sand / tropical green
- not dark hacker
- not neon casino

==================================================
OVERALL STORY FORMAT
==================================================

Create a linear cinematic story.

Flow:

Password Gate
→ Arrival / Ocean Intro
→ First-Person Table View
→ Scene 1: Player Lifecycle
→ Scene 2: Provider Influence
→ Scene 3: KYC
→ Scene 4: Fraud Awareness
→ Scene 5: Bonus Mechanics
→ Scene 6: Payments / Cashier
→ Scene 7: Risk & Compliance
→ Final Hand
→ CV Folder Reveal
→ CV Pages
→ Contact / Replay

The user should not freely move around.
Use a fixed first-person camera with controlled cinematic camera movements.

==================================================
VISUAL DIRECTION
==================================================

The scene is 3D, first-person, warm, light, tropical, premium, and cinematic.

Visual mood:
- tropical terrace
- ocean in the distance
- warm daylight or soft sunset
- palm leaves
- warm wooden table
- whiskey glass
- paper dollars
- elegant cups
- subtle shadows
- soft depth
- calm luxury
- mature private game atmosphere

Important:
The “noir” should exist in the dialogue and jokes only.
The visual background should be warm and light, not dark noir.

Avoid:
- dark cyber/hacker theme
- neon casino
- childish arcade style
- heavy black UI
- loud comedy
- large text blocks during gameplay
- visible candidate/CV content before the final folder reveal

The game should look like:
“a private product conversation disguised as a shell game.”

==================================================
3D SCENE COMPOSITION
==================================================

Create a first-person table scene.

Camera:
- fixed seated position
- looks slightly downward at table
- can slowly pan/tilt during story moments
- should feel like the player is sitting at the table

Recommended camera:
- position: x 0, y 1.25, z -3.2
- rotation: slight downward angle
- FOV: 45–55

Scene objects:
- tropical ocean / terrace background
- palm leaves / greenery
- warm wooden table
- dealer area opposite player
- 3 cups in center
- small ball
- paper dollars near player
- paper dollars near dealer
- whiskey glass near player
- optional cigar case / lighter / small luxury props
- dealer hands
- optional subtle player hands at bottom
- CV folder/documents for final scene

Use placeholder 3D models if needed, but make them visually polished:
- cups should be 3D objects, not flat UI
- money should be paper bills lying on the table
- whiskey glass should be visible in intro and table view
- dealer hands can be stylized 3D models or simplified mesh placeholders

==================================================
MONEY RULES
==================================================

Do NOT show numeric score.
Do NOT show bankroll number.
Do NOT show points.

Money must be physical paper dollars on the table.

Player should see:
- paper dollars near player
- paper dollars near dealer
- money moving physically across the table

Money animations:
- dealer gives dollars to player
- dealer takes dollars from player
- dealer leaves some money
- dealer moves money to pending area
- dealer gives whiskey as soft compensation
- money stack visually grows or shrinks

Use money as a visual story object, not a counter.

==================================================
TEXT RULES DURING GAMEPLAY
==================================================

During gameplay:
- do NOT show candidate information
- do NOT explain the resume
- do NOT show big text blocks
- do NOT show long lessons

Only show:
1. short subtitle dialogue at the bottom
2. small right-corner product insight
3. short interaction prompts

Subtitle style:
- bottom center
- cinematic
- short lines
- speaker name in muted amber
- text in warm white
- dark translucent box
- optional typewriter effect

Right-corner insight style:
- small
- elegant
- subtle
- business/product hint
- not distracting
- changes depending on scene and outcome

==================================================
DIALOGUE STYLE
==================================================

Tone:
- mature
- intelligent
- dry
- noir jokes
- understated humor
- confident
- calm
- not childish
- not clownish
- not too theatrical

Dealer personality:
- smooth
- observant
- ironic
- slightly manipulative
- calm

Player personality:
- sharp
- calm
- capable
- not naive

Examples:
- “Luck is a polite word for weak planning.”
- “Trust is expensive. Friction is too.”
- “You watched the cups. I watched your attention.”
- “A good bonus doesn’t feel desperate.”
- “Verification begins where charm stops working.”

Never mock gambling addiction or vulnerable users.
Jokes should target:
- bad product logic
- weak controls
- unclear requirements
- payment ambiguity
- stakeholder optimism

==================================================
ARRIVAL / OCEAN INTRO
==================================================

Initial scene:
- no text at first
- camera looks far toward the ocean
- warm tropical terrace
- soft ambience
- a hand lifts a whiskey glass
- takes a small sip
- gently places the glass on the wooden table
- camera slowly pans / moves down into the primary table view

Then subtitle appears:

Dealer:
“You’re just in time.”

Camera settles into first-person table view.

==================================================
CORE INTERACTION MODEL
==================================================

Use Babylon.js picking/raycasting.

Interactive objects:
- cups
- dealer hand during fraud scene
- Keep / Switch choice during bonus scene
- Continue prompt
- CV document pages
- Contact buttons via React UI

Interaction rules:
- cups clickable only during choice moments
- dealer hand clickable only during fraud scene
- continue button advances after each scene result
- keep/switch buttons appear only during bonus scene
- CV pages turn with Next / Previous
- replay restarts story after password remains unlocked
- no numeric score
- money changes physically

==================================================
SCENE 1 — PLAYER LIFECYCLE
==================================================

Product domain:
Player lifecycle / retention / return behavior

Setup:
Dealer starts shaking / sliding the cups.

Dialogue:
Dealer: “How long has it been?”
Player: “Three… four months, maybe.”
Dealer: “Long enough to forget the odds. Not long enough to forget the feeling.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: Lifecycle Insight
Text: Returning players are shaped by timing, previous experience, offer relevance, and friction.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

If correct:
- reveal ball
- dealer gives paper dollars to player
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Still sharp. I like that.”
- right-corner insight changes:
Early positive outcomes can increase session intent and willingness to continue.

If wrong:
- dealer takes some money
- leaves some money on player side
- slides or signals an extra whiskey
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Bad luck. Let’s not make it dramatic.”
- right-corner insight changes:
Loss recovery offers can reduce drop-off when they feel personal rather than desperate.

==================================================
SCENE 2 — PROVIDER INFLUENCE
==================================================

Product domain:
Provider quality / game content / partner performance

Dialogue:
Dealer: “Do you remember who introduced us?”
Player: “I remember enough.”
Dealer: “Good. Some introductions are worth keeping. Some are just traffic with a logo.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: Provider Insight
Text: Provider quality affects session depth, discovery, trust, and content performance.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer gives money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Good choice. Some names know how to keep a table busy.”
- insight:
Strong content mix can improve engagement beyond acquisition traffic.

Wrong:
- dealer takes money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Not every shiny table pays for the room.”
- insight:
Weak provider performance can reduce engagement even when acquisition looks healthy.

==================================================
SCENE 3 — KYC
==================================================

Product domain:
KYC / identity / verification / friction / trust

Dialogue:
Player: “Do you even know who I am?”
Dealer: “Enough to let you sit. Not enough to let you disappear.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: KYC Insight
Text: Verification is a trust layer, but poor timing and friction can damage conversion.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer gives money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Clean papers. Clean hands. Rare combination.”

Wrong:
- dealer takes money or delays payout
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Identity is easy. Trust is expensive.”

Hidden product meaning:
KYC is not only compliance. It affects conversion, trust, and continuation.

==================================================
SCENE 4 — FRAUD AWARENESS
==================================================

Product domain:
Fraud / abuse cases / suspicious behavior / misdirection

Important:
No falling-ball mechanic.

New mechanic:
Dealer uses tricky hands and secretly hides the ball in his hand.

Player can click:
1. a cup
2. the dealer’s hand

If player clicks the hand:
- dealer reveals the ball in his hand
- no money is taken
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Checking my hands? Cute.”
Dealer: “Good. You were watching the system, not the decoration.”
- insight:
Fraud often happens outside the obvious user path. Detection depends on behavior, timing, and anomalies.

If player clicks a cup:
- dealer opens hand and shows the ball was never under the cups
- dealer laughs softly
- no money is taken
- subtitle:
Dealer: “You watched the cups.”
Dealer: “I watched your attention.”
- insight:
Fraud patterns often hide in transitions, exceptions, and trusted flows.

Meaning:
This scene teaches that fraud is about attention, misdirection, abuse paths, and suspicious behavior outside the obvious interface.

==================================================
SCENE 5 — BONUS MECHANICS
==================================================

Product domain:
Bonus design / incentive logic / choice architecture

Setup:
Player chooses a cup.

Then dealer slowly lifts another cup slightly and offers a second decision.

Dialogue:
Dealer: “You can keep what you chose.”
Dealer: “Or make it interesting.”

Player choices:
- Keep
- Switch

If player keeps:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Discipline. Rare quality.”
- insight:
A good bonus respects player confidence without forcing unnecessary risk.

If player switches:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition. Expensive habit.”
- insight:
Bonus design balances excitement, cost, abuse risk, and long-term player value.

If switch wins:
- dealer gives more money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambitious. I respect that.”

If switch loses:
- dealer takes some money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition sends invoices.”

==================================================
SCENE 6 — PAYMENTS / CASHIER
==================================================

Product domain:
Payments / cashier / withdrawal logic

Dialogue:
Player: “You pay immediately?”
Dealer: “Only when the system knows what it owes.”

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer pushes dollars clearly across table
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Fast payout. Dangerous thing. People start trusting you.”
- insight:
Clear payout states build trust and reduce support pressure.

Wrong:
- money stays in the middle / pending area
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Pending.”
Player: “That sounds expensive.”
Dealer: “Usually for support.”
- insight:
Every unclear payment state becomes support load: pending, approved, declined, reversed, refunded, manual review.

Required states to show or mention in insight:
- pending
- approved
- declined
- reversed
- refunded
- manual review

==================================================
SCENE 7 — RISK & COMPLIANCE
==================================================

Product domain:
Risk, compliance, auditability

Dialogue:
Dealer: “Rules are boring until someone asks for proof.”
Player: “And then?”
Dealer: “Then boring becomes expensive.”

Interaction:
Short shell-game decision or document/card choice.

Insight:
Good product logic leaves evidence: decisions, states, actions, ownership, and audit trails.

Money movement:
Keep subtle.
If correct, dealer taps the table and leaves money untouched.
If wrong, one dollar moves to a “review” area.

==================================================
FINAL HAND
==================================================

Product domain:
Judgment / product decision-making

Dialogue:
Dealer: “One last hand.”
Player: “For money?”
Dealer: “For judgment.”

Run one final quick cup choice.

After result:
Dealer: “The game is over.”
Dealer: “The product questions are not.”

Dealer places a folder on the table.

==================================================
CV FOLDER REVEAL
==================================================

After gameplay, the CV appears.

This is the first place where more text is acceptable.

Animation:
- dealer places a folder on the table
- folder has stamp:
CONFIDENTIAL
PRODUCT BA PROFILE
- player can click “Next Page”
- page turns / slides / flips
- each page looks like a physical document
- NDA stamps appear on some sections
- text can be longer here

Subtitle:
Dealer: “Take a look.”
Dealer: “Tell me if this man fits the job.”

NDA humor:
Dealer: “He keeps secrets.”
Dealer: “Useful, if your business has sensitive corners.”

==================================================
CV PAGE CONTENT
==================================================

Page 1 — Profile

Business Analyst / Product BA
iGaming / high-risk digital products

- 10+ years in complex technical environments
- Master’s degree in Cybersecurity
- B2 English
- NDA-safe communication style
- Experience leading development and creating complex product-like scenarios

Page 2 — iGaming Fit

- Systems thinking
- Product risk thinking
- Requirements clarity
- Stakeholder alignment
- Abuse-case analysis
- Delivery ownership
- Adaptation under changing requirements

Page 3 — Product Domains

- Player lifecycle
- Provider influence
- KYC / compliance
- Fraud and abuse logic
- Bonus mechanics
- Payments and cashier
- Backoffice / admin tools
- Metrics and reporting

Page 4 — Delivery Style

- Convert ambiguity into structured requirements
- Write acceptance criteria
- Create diagrams and stakeholder-readable decisions
- Lead delivery under changing conditions
- Take responsibility for outcomes
- Balance business, UX, risk, and technical constraints

Page 5 — NDA / Trust

- NDA-protected projects
- No confidential disclosure
- Experience translated into product value without exposing private details
- Can communicate achievements without revealing sensitive implementation details

Page 6 — Contact

Email:
volk.na.oxote@gmail.com

Buttons:
- Send Email
- Replay Story
- Download CV placeholder

==================================================
BABYLON.JS IMPLEMENTATION DETAILS
==================================================

Create modular code.

Suggested structure:

src/
App.tsx or App.jsx
main.tsx or main.jsx
index.css

engine/
createEngine.ts
createScene.ts
webgpuSupport.ts
assetLoader.ts

TableScene.ts

Lighting.ts
Environment.ts
Cups.ts
DealerHands.ts
MoneySystem.ts
WhiskeyGlass.ts
CVFolder3D.ts
Picking.ts

storyState.ts
storyScenes.ts
StoryController.ts
sceneActions.ts

PasswordGate.tsx
SubtitleBar.tsx
InsightCard.tsx
InteractionPrompt.tsx
CVDocumentOverlay.tsx
ContactPanel.tsx
RendererFallback.tsx

utils/
crypto.ts
easing.ts

If TypeScript adds too much complexity, use JavaScript with the same logical structure.

==================================================
3D ASSETS / PLACEHOLDERS
==================================================

If real models are unavailable, create polished procedural placeholders:

Cups:
- use Babylon mesh primitives
- cylinder/frustum style
- metallic/ceramic material
- rounded illusion with highlights

Table:
- box mesh with warm wood material
- subtle procedural texture

Money:
- thin rectangular planes/boxes
- paper dollar texture-like green material
- stacked with slight offsets

Whiskey:
- transparent glass cylinder
- amber liquid cylinder
- subtle highlight

Ball:
- small glossy sphere

Hands:
- stylized simplified mesh placeholders
- acceptable as simple rig-like shapes
- should still move convincingly

CV documents:
- thin paper planes
- folder plane/box
- stamped labels as textures or React overlay aligned to screen

Environment:
- skybox or large background planes
- tropical ocean image placeholder using gradients if no assets
- palm silhouettes / soft background layers

==================================================
ANIMATION REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

Use Babylon animation system or custom tweening.

Required animations:
- arrival camera pan from ocean to table
- whiskey glass lift/sip/place animation
- cup shuffle animation
- dealer hand movement during shuffle
- cup lift animation
- money slide to player
- money removed from player
- money moved to pending area
- fraud hand reveal
- bonus keep/switch reveal
- final folder placement
- document page turn/slide

Animations should feel smooth, cinematic, and intentional.

No teleporting objects unless hidden by camera/misdirection.

==================================================
ADVANCED GUI REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

The GUI must look premium.

Include:
- animated subtitle bar
- right-corner insight card
- smooth scene transitions
- hover/click effects
- subtle vignette
- soft blur panels
- interaction prompts
- CV document overlays
- responsive layout
- mobile fallback warning if needed

Do not make it look like plain HTML buttons.

==================================================
GITHUB PAGES DEPLOYMENT
==================================================

Add or update:

vite.config.js

Use:

import { defineConfig } from 'vite'
import react from '@vitejs/plugin-react'

export default defineConfig({
plugins: [react()],
base: '/igaming-shell-cv/',
})

Add GitHub Actions workflow:

.github/workflows/deploy.yml

Use:
- actions/checkout@v4
- actions/setup-node@v4
- actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
- actions/deploy-pages@v4

Workflow:
- trigger on push to main
- npm ci
- npm run build
- upload dist
- deploy to GitHub Pages

==================================================
PACKAGE DEPENDENCIES
==================================================

Install:
- react
- react-dom
- vite
- @vitejs/plugin-react
- typescript if using TS
- tailwindcss
- postcss
- autoprefixer
- @babylonjs/core
- @babylonjs/loaders
- framer-motion
- lucide-react

If Tailwind is not configured, configure it.

tailwind.config.js should include:

content: [
"./index.html",
"./src/**/*.{js,jsx,ts,tsx}",
]

src/index.css should include:

@tailwind base;
@tailwind components;
@tailwind utilities;

- dealer hands can be stylized 3D models or simplified mesh placeholders

==================================================
MONEY RULES
==================================================

Do NOT show numeric score.
Do NOT show bankroll number.
Do NOT show points.

Money must be physical paper dollars on the table.

Player should see:
- paper dollars near player
- paper dollars near dealer
- money moving physically across the table

Money animations:
- dealer gives dollars to player
- dealer takes dollars from player
- dealer leaves some money
- dealer moves money to pending area
- dealer gives whiskey as soft compensation
- money stack visually grows or shrinks

Use money as a visual story object, not a counter.

==================================================
TEXT RULES DURING GAMEPLAY
==================================================

During gameplay:
- do NOT show candidate information
- do NOT explain the resume
- do NOT show big text blocks
- do NOT show long lessons

Only show:
1. short subtitle dialogue at the bottom
2. small right-corner product insight
3. short interaction prompts

Subtitle style:
- bottom center
- cinematic
- short lines
- speaker name in muted amber
- text in warm white
- dark translucent box
- optional typewriter effect

Right-corner insight style:
- small
- elegant
- subtle
- business/product hint
- not distracting
- changes depending on scene and outcome

==================================================
DIALOGUE STYLE
==================================================

Tone:
- mature
- intelligent
- dry
- noir jokes
- understated humor
- confident
- calm
- not childish
- not clownish
- not too theatrical

Dealer personality:
- smooth
- observant
- ironic
- slightly manipulative
- calm

Player personality:
- sharp
- calm
- capable
- not naive

Examples:
- “Luck is a polite word for weak planning.”
- “Trust is expensive. Friction is too.”
- “You watched the cups. I watched your attention.”
- “A good bonus doesn’t feel desperate.”
- “Verification begins where charm stops working.”

Never mock gambling addiction or vulnerable users.
Jokes should target:
- bad product logic
- weak controls
- unclear requirements
- payment ambiguity
- stakeholder optimism

==================================================
ARRIVAL / OCEAN INTRO
==================================================

Initial scene:
- no text at first
- camera looks far toward the ocean
- warm tropical terrace
- soft ambience
- a hand lifts a whiskey glass
- takes a small sip
- gently places the glass on the wooden table
- camera slowly pans / moves down into the primary table view

Then subtitle appears:

Dealer:
“You’re just in time.”

Camera settles into first-person table view.

==================================================
CORE INTERACTION MODEL
==================================================

Use Babylon.js picking/raycasting.

Interactive objects:
- cups
- dealer hand during fraud scene
- Keep / Switch choice during bonus scene
- Continue prompt
- CV document pages
- Contact buttons via React UI

Interaction rules:
- cups clickable only during choice moments
- dealer hand clickable only during fraud scene
- continue button advances after each scene result
- keep/switch buttons appear only during bonus scene
- CV pages turn with Next / Previous
- replay restarts story after password remains unlocked
- no numeric score
- money changes physically

==================================================
SCENE 1 — PLAYER LIFECYCLE
==================================================

Product domain:
Player lifecycle / retention / return behavior

Setup:
Dealer starts shaking / sliding the cups.

Dialogue:
Dealer: “How long has it been?”
Player: “Three… four months, maybe.”
Dealer: “Long enough to forget the odds. Not long enough to forget the feeling.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: Lifecycle Insight
Text: Returning players are shaped by timing, previous experience, offer relevance, and friction.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

If correct:
- reveal ball
- dealer gives paper dollars to player
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Still sharp. I like that.”
- right-corner insight changes:
Early positive outcomes can increase session intent and willingness to continue.

If wrong:
- dealer takes some money
- leaves some money on player side
- slides or signals an extra whiskey
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Bad luck. Let’s not make it dramatic.”
- right-corner insight changes:
Loss recovery offers can reduce drop-off when they feel personal rather than desperate.

==================================================
SCENE 2 — PROVIDER INFLUENCE
==================================================

Product domain:
Provider quality / game content / partner performance

Dialogue:
Dealer: “Do you remember who introduced us?”
Player: “I remember enough.”
Dealer: “Good. Some introductions are worth keeping. Some are just traffic with a logo.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: Provider Insight
Text: Provider quality affects session depth, discovery, trust, and content performance.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer gives money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Good choice. Some names know how to keep a table busy.”
- insight:
Strong content mix can improve engagement beyond acquisition traffic.

Wrong:
- dealer takes money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Not every shiny table pays for the room.”
- insight:
Weak provider performance can reduce engagement even when acquisition looks healthy.

==================================================
SCENE 3 — KYC
==================================================

Product domain:
KYC / identity / verification / friction / trust

Dialogue:
Player: “Do you even know who I am?”
Dealer: “Enough to let you sit. Not enough to let you disappear.”

Right-corner insight:
Title: KYC Insight
Text: Verification is a trust layer, but poor timing and friction can damage conversion.

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer gives money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Clean papers. Clean hands. Rare combination.”

Wrong:
- dealer takes money or delays payout
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Identity is easy. Trust is expensive.”

Hidden product meaning:
KYC is not only compliance. It affects conversion, trust, and continuation.

==================================================
SCENE 4 — FRAUD AWARENESS
==================================================

Product domain:
Fraud / abuse cases / suspicious behavior / misdirection

Important:
No falling-ball mechanic.

New mechanic:
Dealer uses tricky hands and secretly hides the ball in his hand.

Player can click:
1. a cup
2. the dealer’s hand

If player clicks the hand:
- dealer reveals the ball in his hand
- no money is taken
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Checking my hands? Cute.”
Dealer: “Good. You were watching the system, not the decoration.”
- insight:
Fraud often happens outside the obvious user path. Detection depends on behavior, timing, and anomalies.

If player clicks a cup:
- dealer opens hand and shows the ball was never under the cups
- dealer laughs softly
- no money is taken
- subtitle:
Dealer: “You watched the cups.”
Dealer: “I watched your attention.”
- insight:
Fraud patterns often hide in transitions, exceptions, and trusted flows.

Meaning:
This scene teaches that fraud is about attention, misdirection, abuse paths, and suspicious behavior outside the obvious interface.

==================================================
SCENE 5 — BONUS MECHANICS
==================================================

Product domain:
Bonus design / incentive logic / choice architecture

Setup:
Player chooses a cup.

Then dealer slowly lifts another cup slightly and offers a second decision.

Dialogue:
Dealer: “You can keep what you chose.”
Dealer: “Or make it interesting.”

Player choices:
- Keep
- Switch

If player keeps:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Discipline. Rare quality.”
- insight:
A good bonus respects player confidence without forcing unnecessary risk.

If player switches:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition. Expensive habit.”
- insight:
Bonus design balances excitement, cost, abuse risk, and long-term player value.

If switch wins:
- dealer gives more money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambitious. I respect that.”

If switch loses:
- dealer takes some money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition sends invoices.”

==================================================
SCENE 6 — PAYMENTS / CASHIER
==================================================

Product domain:
Payments / cashier / withdrawal logic

Dialogue:
Player: “You pay immediately?”
Dealer: “Only when the system knows what it owes.”

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer pushes dollars clearly across table
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Fast payout. Dangerous thing. People start trusting you.”
- insight:
Clear payout states build trust and reduce support pressure.

Wrong:
- money stays in the middle / pending area
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Pending.”
Player: “That sounds expensive.”
Dealer: “Usually for support.”
- insight:
Every unclear payment state becomes support load: pending, approved, declined, reversed, refunded, manual review.

Required states to show or mention in insight:
- pending
- approved
- declined
- reversed
- refunded
- manual review

==================================================
SCENE 7 — RISK & COMPLIANCE
==================================================

Product domain:
Risk, compliance, auditability

Dialogue:
Dealer: “Rules are boring until someone asks for proof.”
Player: “And then?”
Dealer: “Then boring becomes expensive.”

Interaction:
Short shell-game decision or document/card choice.

Insight:
Good product logic leaves evidence: decisions, states, actions, ownership, and audit trails.

Money movement:
Keep subtle.
If correct, dealer taps the table and leaves money untouched.
If wrong, one dollar moves to a “review” area.

==================================================
FINAL HAND
==================================================

Product domain:
Judgment / product decision-making

Dialogue:
Dealer: “One last hand.”
Player: “For money?”
Dealer: “For judgment.”

Run one final quick cup choice.

After result:
Dealer: “The game is over.”
Dealer: “The product questions are not.”

Dealer places a folder on the table.

==================================================
CV FOLDER REVEAL
==================================================

After gameplay, the CV appears.

This is the first place where more text is acceptable.

Animation:
- dealer places a folder on the table
- folder has stamp:
CONFIDENTIAL
PRODUCT BA PROFILE
- player can click “Next Page”
- page turns / slides / flips
- each page looks like a physical document
- NDA stamps appear on some sections
- text can be longer here

Subtitle:
Dealer: “Take a look.”
Dealer: “Tell me if this man fits the job.”

NDA humor:
Dealer: “He keeps secrets.”
Dealer: “Useful, if your business has sensitive corners.”

==================================================
CV PAGE CONTENT
==================================================

Page 1 — Profile

Business Analyst / Product BA
iGaming / high-risk digital products

- 10+ years in complex technical environments
- Master’s degree in Cybersecurity
- B2 English
- NDA-safe communication style
- Experience leading development and creating complex product-like scenarios

Page 2 — iGaming Fit

- Systems thinking
- Product risk thinking
- Requirements clarity
- Stakeholder alignment
- Abuse-case analysis
- Delivery ownership
- Adaptation under changing requirements

Page 3 — Product Domains

- Player lifecycle
- Provider influence
- KYC / compliance
- Fraud and abuse logic
- Bonus mechanics
- Payments and cashier
- Backoffice / admin tools
- Metrics and reporting

Page 4 — Delivery Style

- Convert ambiguity into structured requirements
- Write acceptance criteria
- Create diagrams and stakeholder-readable decisions
- Lead delivery under changing conditions
- Take responsibility for outcomes
- Balance business, UX, risk, and technical constraints

Page 5 — NDA / Trust

- NDA-protected projects
- No confidential disclosure
- Experience translated into product value without exposing private details
- Can communicate achievements without revealing sensitive implementation details

Page 6 — Contact

Email:
volk.na.oxote@gmail.com

Buttons:
- Send Email
- Replay Story
- Download CV placeholder

BABYLON.JS IMPLEMENTATION DETAILS

index.css

CVDocumentOverlay.tsx
ContactPanel.tsx
RendererFallback.tsx

crypto.ts
easing.ts

If TypeScript adds too much complexity, use JavaScript with the same logical structure.

==================================================
3D ASSETS / PLACEHOLDERS
==================================================

If real models are unavailable, create polished procedural placeholders:

Cups:
- use Babylon mesh primitives
- cylinder/frustum style
- metallic/ceramic material
- rounded illusion with highlights

Table:
- box mesh with warm wood material
- subtle procedural texture

Money:
- thin rectangular planes/boxes
- paper dollar texture-like green material
- stacked with slight offsets

Whiskey:
- transparent glass cylinder
- amber liquid cylinder
- subtle highlight

Ball:
- small glossy sphere

Hands:
- stylized simplified mesh placeholders
- acceptable as simple rig-like shapes
- should still move convincingly

CV documents:
- thin paper planes
- folder plane/box
- stamped labels as textures or React overlay aligned to screen

Environment:
- skybox or large background planes
- tropical ocean image placeholder using gradients if no assets
- palm silhouettes / soft background layers

==================================================
ANIMATION REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

Use Babylon animation system or custom tweening.

Required animations:
- arrival camera pan from ocean to table
- whiskey glass lift/sip/place animation
- cup shuffle animation
- dealer hand movement during shuffle
- cup lift animation
- money slide to player
- money removed from player
- money moved to pending area
- fraud hand reveal
- bonus keep/switch reveal
- final folder placement
- document page turn/slide

Animations should feel smooth, cinematic, and intentional.

No teleporting objects unless hidden by camera/misdirection.

==================================================
ADVANCED GUI REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

The GUI must look premium.

Include:
- animated subtitle bar
- right-corner insight card
- smooth scene transitions
- hover/click effects
- subtle vignette
- soft blur panels
- interaction prompts
- CV document overlays
- responsive layout
- mobile fallback warning if needed

Do not make it look like plain HTML buttons.

==================================================
GITHUB PAGES DEPLOYMENT
==================================================

Add or update:

vite.config.js

Use:

import { defineConfig } from 'vite'
import react from '@vitejs/plugin-react'

export default defineConfig({
plugins: [react()],
base: '/igaming-shell-cv/',
})

Add GitHub Actions workflow:

.github/workflows/deploy.yml

Use:
- actions/checkout@v4
- actions/setup-node@v4
- actions/upload-pages-artifact@v3
- actions/deploy-pages@v4

Workflow:
- trigger on push to main
- npm ci
- npm run build
- upload dist
- deploy to GitHub Pages

==================================================
PACKAGE DEPENDENCIES
==================================================

Install:
- react
- react-dom
- vite
- @vitejs/plugin-react
- typescript if using TS
- tailwindcss
- postcss
- autoprefixer

- @babylonjs/loaders
- framer-motion
- lucide-react

If Tailwind is not configured, configure it.

tailwind.config.js should include:

content: [
"./index.html",
"./src/**/*.{js,jsx,ts,tsx}",
]

src/index.css should include:

@tailwind base;
@tailwind components;
@tailwind utilities;

==================================================
ACCEPTANCE CRITERIA
==================================================

The final project is acceptable if:

- Password gate appears first
- Correct password unlocks the story
- WebGPU renderer is attempted first
- WebGL fallback works if WebGPU is unavailable
- Experience is 3D first-person, not flat UI
- Background is warm, tropical, premium, and light
- Noir exists in dialogue only, not as a dark visual theme
- Intro starts by looking at ocean
- Whiskey glass is lifted, sipped, and placed on table
- Camera transitions to first-person table view
- Dealer and player communicate through short subtitles
- No candidate info appears during gameplay
- Right-corner product insights appear subtly
- Money is physical paper dollars on the table
- No numeric score or bankroll is shown
- Each scene represents a product domain
- Fraud scene lets player click either cup or dealer hand
- Bonus scene offers keep/switch choice
- CV appears only at the end as a confidential folder/documents
- CV pages include NDA/confidential marks
- Contact page includes volk.na.oxote@gmail.com
- App builds with npm run build
- GitHub Pages workflow is included

==================================================
IMPORTANT VISUAL PRIORITY
==================================================

Do not implement this as a basic React card layout.

The main value is the 3D cinematic table scene:
- ocean intro
- whiskey
- warm table
- cups
- dealer hands
- paper dollars
- subtle misdirection
- final CV folder

React UI should support the story, not replace the scene.Create a WebGPU-first 3D interactive web experience.

Project title:
“Guess the Cup. Read the Product.”

Goal:
Build a cinematic first-person 3D shell-game story that works as a creative CV / product case presentation for an iGaming Business Analyst / Product BA candidate.

This should NOT be a normal resume website.
This should NOT be an arcade game.
This should NOT be a neon casino UI.

It should feel like:
- a private tropical table game
- a warm cinematic product conversation
- a magic trick with misdirection
- noir humor in dialogue only
- advanced WebGPU/WebGL 3D scene
- subtle business/product insights
- CV revealed only at the end as documents on the table

==================================================
TECH STACK
==================================================

Use:

- React
- Vite
- TypeScript if practical, otherwise JavaScript
- Babylon.js for 3D scene
- WebGPU-first rendering
- WebGL fallback if WebGPU is unavailable
- Tailwind CSS for UI overlays
- Framer Motion for UI transitions
- lucide-react only for small UI icons if needed

The 3D scene must be handled by Babylon.js.
React should handle:
- password gate
- subtitles
- right-corner insight cards
- interaction prompts
- CV document text overlays
- contact buttons

The app must be static and deployable to GitHub Pages.

Repository name:

igaming-shell-cv

Use this in vite.config.js:

base: '/igaming-shell-cv/'

==================================================
WEBGPU / WEBGL REQUIREMENT
==================================================

Implement rendering like this:

1. Try to initialize Babylon.js WebGPU engine.
2. If WebGPU is unavailable, gracefully fall back to Babylon.js WebGL engine.
3. If neither works, show a polished fallback message:
“Your browser cannot run this private table. Try a modern desktop browser.”

Important:
Do not make WebGPU-only with no fallback.

Show a tiny non-intrusive technical badge only if needed:
- “WebGPU mode”
- “WebGL fallback mode”

But keep it subtle.

==================================================
PASSWORD GATE
==================================================

Before the story starts, show a full-screen password screen.

Title:
Private Product Demo

Subtitle:
A small shell game about iGaming product logic, risk, payments, and requirements.

Password:
iGamingBA2026!

Do NOT show the password visibly.

Use SHA-256 comparison with browser Web Crypto API.

SHA-256 hash:
2834c295eb954847ae5538f997d4970ce4b55fc07d8ad400a73d2a7ea335de0a

If correct:
- store unlocked state in sessionStorage
- show the story

If wrong:
show error:
“Wrong cup. Wrong password. Product risk detected.”

Microcopy:
“Demo access only.”

Add comment near password logic:
“Frontend password protection is only a demo barrier for static hosting. Do not use this for sensitive or NDA-protected information.”

Password page visual style:
- warm tropical
- glassmorphism
- elegant
- soft light
- muted amber / sand / tropical green
- not dark hacker
- not neon casino

==================================================
OVERALL STORY FORMAT
==================================================

Create a linear cinematic story.

Flow:

Password Gate
→ Arrival / Ocean Intro
→ First-Person Table View
→ Scene 1: Player Lifecycle
→ Scene 2: Provider Influence
→ Scene 3: KYC
→ Scene 4: Fraud Awareness
→ Scene 5: Bonus Mechanics
→ Scene 6: Payments / Cashier
→ Scene 7: Risk & Compliance
→ Final Hand
→ CV Folder Reveal
→ CV Pages
→ Contact / Replay

The user should not freely move around.
Use a fixed first-person camera with controlled cinematic camera movements.

==================================================
VISUAL DIRECTION
==================================================

The scene is 3D, first-person, warm, light, tropical, premium, and cinematic.

Visual mood:
- tropical terrace
- ocean in the distance
- warm daylight or soft sunset
- palm leaves
- warm wooden table
- whiskey glass
- paper dollars
- elegant cups
- subtle shadows
- soft depth
- calm luxury
- mature private game atmosphere

Important:
The “noir” should exist in the dialogue and jokes only.
The visual background should be warm and light, not dark noir.

Avoid:
- dark cyber/hacker theme
- neon casino
- childish arcade style
- heavy black UI
- loud comedy
- large text blocks during gameplay
- visible candidate/CV content before the final folder reveal

The game should look like:
“a private product conversation disguised as a shell game.”

==================================================
3D SCENE COMPOSITION
==================================================

Create a first-person table scene.

Camera:
- fixed seated position
- looks slightly downward at table
- can slowly pan/tilt during story moments
- should feel like the player is sitting at the table

Recommended camera:
- position: x 0, y 1.25, z -3.2
- rotation: slight downward angle
- FOV: 45–55

Scene objects:
- tropical ocean / terrace background
- palm leaves / greenery
- warm wooden table
- dealer area opposite player
- 3 cups in center
- small ball
- paper dollars near player
- paper dollars near dealer
- whiskey glass near player
- optional cigar case / lighter / small luxury props
- dealer hands
- optional subtle player hands at bottom
- CV folder/documents for final scene

Use placeholder 3D models if needed, but make them visually polished:
- cups should be 3D objects, not flat UI
- money should be paper bills lying on the table
- whiskey glass should be visible in intro and table view
- dealer hands can be stylized 3D models or simplified mesh placeholders

- insight:
Fraud patterns often hide in transitions, exceptions, and trusted flows.

Meaning:
This scene teaches that fraud is about attention, misdirection, abuse paths, and suspicious behavior outside the obvious interface.

==================================================
SCENE 5 — BONUS MECHANICS
==================================================

Product domain:
Bonus design / incentive logic / choice architecture

Setup:
Player chooses a cup.

Then dealer slowly lifts another cup slightly and offers a second decision.

Dialogue:
Dealer: “You can keep what you chose.”
Dealer: “Or make it interesting.”

Player choices:
- Keep
- Switch

If player keeps:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Discipline. Rare quality.”
- insight:
A good bonus respects player confidence without forcing unnecessary risk.

If player switches:
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition. Expensive habit.”
- insight:
Bonus design balances excitement, cost, abuse risk, and long-term player value.

If switch wins:
- dealer gives more money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambitious. I respect that.”

If switch loses:
- dealer takes some money
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Ambition sends invoices.”

==================================================
SCENE 6 — PAYMENTS / CASHIER
==================================================

Product domain:
Payments / cashier / withdrawal logic

Dialogue:
Player: “You pay immediately?”
Dealer: “Only when the system knows what it owes.”

Interaction:
Player chooses a cup.

Correct:
- dealer pushes dollars clearly across table
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Fast payout. Dangerous thing. People start trusting you.”
- insight:
Clear payout states build trust and reduce support pressure.

Wrong:
- money stays in the middle / pending area
- subtitle:
Dealer: “Pending.”
Player: “That sounds expensive.”
Dealer: “Usually for support.”
- insight:
Every unclear payment state becomes support load: pending, approved, declined, reversed, refunded, manual review.

Required states to show or mention in insight:
- pending
- approved
- declined
- reversed
- refunded
- manual review

==================================================
SCENE 7 — RISK & COMPLIANCE
==================================================

Product domain:
Risk, compliance, auditability

Dialogue:
Dealer: “Rules are boring until someone asks for proof.”
Player: “And then?”
Dealer: “Then boring becomes expensive.”

Interaction:
Short shell-game decision or document/card choice.

Insight:
Good product logic leaves evidence: decisions, states, actions, ownership, and audit trails.

Money movement:
Keep subtle.
If correct, dealer taps the table and leaves money untouched.
If wrong, one dollar moves to a “review” area.

==================================================
FINAL HAND
==================================================

Product domain:
Judgment / product decision-making

Dialogue:
Dealer: “One last hand.”
Player: “For money?”
Dealer: “For judgment.”

Run one final quick cup choice.

After result:
Dealer: “The game is over.”
Dealer: “The product questions are not.”

Dealer places a folder on the table.

==================================================
CV FOLDER REVEAL
==================================================

After gameplay, the CV appears.

This is the first place where more text is acceptable.

Animation:
- dealer places a folder on the table
- folder has stamp:
CONFIDENTIAL
PRODUCT BA PROFILE
- player can click “Next Page”
- page turns / slides / flips
- each page looks like a physical document
- NDA stamps appear on some sections
- text can be longer here

Subtitle:
Dealer: “Take a look.”
Dealer: “Tell me if this man fits the job.”

NDA humor:
Dealer: “He keeps secrets.”
Dealer: “Useful, if your business has sensitive corners.”

==================================================
3D ASSETS / PLACEHOLDERS
==================================================

If real models are unavailable, create polished procedural placeholders:

Cups:
- use Babylon mesh primitives
- cylinder/frustum style
- metallic/ceramic material
- rounded illusion with highlights

Table:
- box mesh with warm wood material
- subtle procedural texture

Money:
- thin rectangular planes/boxes
- paper dollar texture-like green material
- stacked with slight offsets

Whiskey:
- transparent glass cylinder
- amber liquid cylinder
- subtle highlight

Ball:
- small glossy sphere

Hands:
- stylized simplified mesh placeholders
- acceptable as simple rig-like shapes
- should still move convincingly

CV documents:
- thin paper planes
- folder plane/box
- stamped labels as textures or React overlay aligned to screen

Environment:
- skybox or large background planes
- tropical ocean image placeholder using gradients if no assets
- palm silhouettes / soft background layers

==================================================
ANIMATION REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

Use Babylon animation system or custom tweening.

Required animations:
- arrival camera pan from ocean to table
- whiskey glass lift/sip/place animation
- cup shuffle animation
- dealer hand movement during shuffle
- cup lift animation
- money slide to player
- money removed from player
- money moved to pending area
- fraud hand reveal
- bonus keep/switch reveal
- final folder placement
- document page turn/slide

Animations should feel smooth, cinematic, and intentional.

No teleporting objects unless hidden by camera/misdirection.

==================================================
ADVANCED GUI REQUIREMENTS
==================================================

The GUI must look premium.

Include:
- animated subtitle bar
- right-corner insight card
- smooth scene transitions
- hover/click effects
- subtle vignette
- soft blur panels
- interaction prompts
- CV document overlays
- responsive layout
- mobile fallback warning if needed

Do not make it look like plain HTML buttons.

import { defineConfig } from 'vite'

.github/workflows/deploy.yml

Workflow:
- trigger on push to main
- npm ci
- npm run build
- upload dist
- deploy to GitHub Pages
